      38                 :            : /* ----------
      39                 :            :  * Uncomment the following to enable compilation of dump_numeric()
      40                 :            :  * and dump_var() and to get a dump of any result produced by make_result().
      41                 :            :  * ----------
      42                 :            : #define NUMERIC_DEBUG
      43                 :            :  */
      44                 :            : 
      45                 :            : 
      46                 :            : /* ----------
      47                 :            :  * Local data types
      48                 :            :  *
      49                 :            :  * Numeric values are represented in a base-NBASE floating point format.
      50                 :            :  * Each "digit" ranges from 0 to NBASE-1.  The type NumericDigit is signed
      51                 :            :  * and wide enough to store a digit.  We assume that NBASE*NBASE can fit in
      52                 :            :  * an int.      Although the purely calculational routines could handle any even
      53                 :            :  * NBASE that's less than sqrt(INT_MAX), in practice we are only interested
      54                 :            :  * in NBASE a power of ten, so that I/O conversions and decimal rounding
      55                 :            :  * are easy.  Also, it's actually more efficient if NBASE is rather less than
      56                 :            :  * sqrt(INT_MAX), so that there is "headroom" for mul_var and div_var to
      57                 :            :  * postpone processing carries.
      58                 :            :  * ----------
      59                 :            :  */
      60                 :            : 
      61                 :            : 
      62                 :            : #if 1
      63                 :            : #define NBASE           10000
      64                 :            : #define HALF_NBASE      5000
      65                 :            : #define DEC_DIGITS      4                       /* decimal digits per NBASE digit */
      66                 :            : #define MUL_GUARD_DIGITS        2       /* these are measured in NBASE digits */
      67                 :            : #define DIV_GUARD_DIGITS        4
      68                 :            : 
      69                 :            : typedef int16 NumericDigit;
      70                 :            : #endif
      71                 :            : 
      72                 :            : 
      73                 :            : /* ----------
      74                 :            :  * NumericVar is the format we use for arithmetic.      The digit-array part
      75                 :            :  * is the same as the NumericData storage format, but the header is more
      76                 :            :  * complex.
      77                 :            :  *
      78                 :            :  * The value represented by a NumericVar is determined by the sign, weight,
      79                 :            :  * ndigits, and digits[] array.
      80                 :            :  * Note: the first digit of a NumericVar's value is assumed to be multiplied
      81                 :            :  * by NBASE ** weight.  Another way to say it is that there are weight+1
      82                 :            :  * digits before the decimal point.  It is possible to have weight < 0.
      83                 :            :  *
      84                 :            :  * buf: points at the physical start of the digit buffer for the NumericVar.
      85                 :            :  * This is either the local buffer (ndb) or a palloc'd buffer.
      86                 :            :  *
      87                 :            :  * digits: points at the first digit in actual use (the one with the
      88                 :            :  * specified weight).   We normally leave an unused digit or two
      89                 :            :  * (preset to zeroes) between buf and digits, so that there is room to store
      90                 :            :  * a carry out of the top digit without special pushups.  We just need to
      91                 :            :  * decrement digits (and increment weight) to make room for the carry digit.
      92                 :            :  * (There is no such extra space in a numeric value stored in the database,
      93                 :            :  * only in a NumericVar in memory.)
      94                 :            :  *
      95                 :            :  * If buf is set to ndb, then the digit buffer isn't actually palloc'd and
      96                 :            :  * should not be freed --- see the constants below for an example.
      97                 :            :  *
      98                 :            :  * dscale: display scale, is the nominal precision expressed as number
      99                 :            :  * of digits after the decimal point (it must always be >= 0 at present).
     100                 :            :  * dscale may be more than the number of physically stored fractional digits,
     101                 :            :  * implying that we have suppressed storage of significant trailing zeroes.
     102                 :            :  * It should never be less than the number of stored digits, since that would
     103                 :            :  * imply hiding digits that are present.  NOTE that dscale is always expressed
     104                 :            :  * in *decimal* digits, and so it may correspond to a fractional number of
     105                 :            :  * base-NBASE digits --- divide by DEC_DIGITS to convert to NBASE digits.
     106                 :            :  *
     107                 :            :  * rscale, or result scale, is the target precision for a computation.
     108                 :            :  * Like dscale it is expressed as number of *decimal* digits after the decimal
     109                 :            :  * point, and is always >= 0 at present.
     110                 :            :  * Note that rscale is not stored in variables --- it's figured on-the-fly
     111                 :            :  * from the dscales of the inputs.
     112                 :            :  *
     113                 :            :  * NB: All the variable-level functions are written in a style that makes it
     114                 :            :  * possible to give one and the same variable as argument and destination.
     115                 :            :  *
     116                 :            :  * ----------
     117                 :            :  */
     118                 :            : #define NUMERIC_LOCAL_NDIG      36              /* number of 'digits' in local digits[] */
     119                 :            : #define NUMERIC_LOCAL_NMAX      (NUMERIC_LOCAL_NDIG - 2)
     120                 :            : #define NUMERIC_LOCAL_DTXT      128             /* number of char in local text */
     121                 :            : #define NUMERIC_LOCAL_DMAX      (NUMERIC_LOCAL_DTXT - 2)
     122                 :            : 
     123                 :            : typedef struct NumericVar
     124                 :            : {
     125                 :            :         int                     ndigits;                /* # of digits in digits[] - can be 0! */
     126                 :            :         int                     weight;                 /* weight of first digit */
     127                 :            :         int                     sign;                   /* NUMERIC_POS, NUMERIC_NEG, or NUMERIC_NAN */
     128                 :            :         int                     dscale;                 /* display scale */
     129                 :            :         NumericDigit *buf                       /* start of space for digits[] */;
     130                 :            :         NumericDigit *digits;           /* base-NBASE digits */
     131                 :            :         NumericDigit ndb[NUMERIC_LOCAL_NDIG];   /* local space for digits[] */
     132                 :            : } NumericVar;
     133                 :            : 
     134                 :            : #define NUMERIC_LOCAL_HSIZ      \
     135                 :            :                         (sizeof(NumericVar) - (sizeof(NumericDigit) * NUMERIC_LOCAL_NDIG))
     136                 :            : 
     137                 :            : /* ----------

     907                 :            : /*
     908                 :            :  * Implements the numeric version of the width_bucket() function
     909                 :            :  * defined by SQL2003. See also width_bucket_float8().
     910                 :            :  *

     914                 :            :  * bucket number that 'operand' belongs to in an equiwidth histogram

    2720                 :            :         else
    2721                 :         20 :                 PG_RETURN_NUMERIC(res);
    2722                 :         20 : }
    2723                 :            : 
    2724                 :            : /*
    2725                 :            :  * SUM transition functions for integer datatypes.
    2726                 :            :  *
    2727                 :            :  * To avoid overflow, we use accumulators wider than the input datatype.
    2728                 :            :  * A Numeric accumulator is needed for int8 input; for int4 and int2
    2729                 :            :  * inputs, we use int8 accumulators which should be sufficient for practical
    2730                 :            :  * purposes.  (The latter two therefore don't really belong in this file,
    2731                 :            :  * but we keep them here anyway.)
    2732                 :            :  *
    2733                 :            :  * Because SQL92 defines the SUM() of no values to be NULL, not zero,
    2734                 :            :  * the initial condition of the transition data value needs to be NULL. This
    2735                 :            :  * means we can't rely on ExecAgg to automatically insert the first non-null
    2736                 :            :  * data value into the transition data: it doesn't know how to do the type
